## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/prometheus--ba14bc4 (mirror of prometheus/prometheus)
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

     1→# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure
     2→
     3→## Summary
     4→
     5→The Prometheus remote-write queue system experiences intermittent sample loss and stalled shards during dynamic resharding operations. When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.
     6→
     7→## Root Cause
     8→
     9→### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush
    10→
    11→**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)
    12→
    13→The bug occurs at line 1241:
    14→```go
    15→func (s *shards) start(n int) {
    16→    s.mtx.Lock()
    17→    defer s.mtx.Unlock()
    18→
    19→    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC
    20→    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))
    21→```
    22→
    23→When resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):
    24→```go
    25→case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:
    26→    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards
    27→    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards
    28→```
    29→
    30→The sequence creates a race condition:
    31→
    32→1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):
    33→   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)
    34→   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)
    35→   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)
    36→
    37→2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):
    38→   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)
    39→   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)
    40→   - Samples in queues are lost
    41→
    42→3.
... (truncated)
51-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the investigation of the Prometheus remote-write queue resharding issue. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause**: A race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing in `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`.

**The Bug**: 
- Line 1241 in `shards.start()` unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` metric to 0
- But this happens while old shards are still being flushed during resharding
- If flush times out (> flushDeadline), samples are dropped in the hard shutdown
- The metric reset hides these dropped samples

**Why It's Intermittent**:
- Depends on target discovery timing relative to sample processing
- Depends on remote backend latency (if slow, flush times out)
- Only manifests when resharding occurs under high load

**Why Shards Stall**:
- During resharding, the modulo operation for shard assignment changes with the queue count
- Samples that fail to enqueue during the transition retry later
- They hash to different (potentially overloaded) shards
- Creates uneven load distribution

## Investigation Report

The complete investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with:
- Specific code references (file paths and line numbers)
- Evidence from the resharding logic
- Metrics and logs that confirm the issue
- Reproduction conditions
- Recommended fix strategies with diagnostic steps

The report covers all required sections: Summary, Root Cause, Evidence, Affected Components, and Recommendations for both fixing and diagnosing the issue.

\t\tm.reg.Unregister(m.sentBytesTotal)\n398: \t\tm.reg.Unregister(m.metadataBytesTotal)\n399: \t\tm.reg.Unregister(m.maxSamplesPerSend)\n400: \t}\n401: }\n402: \n403: // WriteClient defines an interface for sending a batch of samples to an\n404: // external timeseries database.\n405: type WriteClient interface {\n406: \t// Store stores the given samples in the remote storage.\n407: \tStore(ctx context.Context, req []byte, retryAttempt int) (WriteResponseStats, error)\n408: \t// Name uniquely identifies the remote storage.\n409: \tName() string\n410: \t// Endpoint is the remote read or write endpoint for the storage client.\n411: \tEndpoint() string\n412: }\n413: \n414: // QueueManager manages a queue of samples to be sent to the Storage\n415: // indicated by the provided WriteClient. Implements writeTo interface\n416: // used by WAL Watcher.\n417: type QueueManager struct {\n418: \tlastSendTimestamp            atomic.Int64\n419: \tbuildRequestLimitTimestamp   atomic.Int64\n420: \treshardDisableStartTimestamp atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard was disabled.\n421: \treshardDisableEndTimestamp   atomic.Int64 // Time that reshard is disabled until.\n422: \n423: \tlogger                  *slog.Logger\n424: \tflushDeadline           time.Duration\n425: \tcfg                     config.QueueConfig\n426: \tmcfg                    config.MetadataConfig\n427: \texternalLabels          []labels.Label\n428: \trelabelConfigs          []*relabel.Config\n429: \tsendExemplars           bool\n430: \tsendNativeHistograms    bool\n431: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool\n432: \twatcher                 *wlog.Watcher\n433: \tmetadataWatcher         *MetadataWatcher\n434: \n435: \tclientMtx   sync.RWMutex\n436: \tstoreClient WriteClient\n437: \tprotoMsg    config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg\n438: \tcompr       compression.Type\n439: \n440: \tseriesMtx      sync.Mutex // Covers seriesLabels, seriesMetadata, droppedSeries and builder.\n441: \tseriesLabels   map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels\n442: \tseriesMetadata map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata\n443: \tdroppedSeries  map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}\n444: \tbuilder        *labels.Builder\n445: \n446: \tseriesSegmentMtx     sync.Mutex // Covers seriesSegmentIndexes - if you also lock seriesMtx, take seriesMtx first.\n447: \tseriesSegmentIndexes map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int\n448: \n449: \tshards      *shards\n450: \tnumShards   int\n451: \treshardChan chan int\n452: \tquit        chan struct{}\n453: \twg          sync.WaitGroup\n454: \n455: \tdataIn, dataOut, dataOutDuration *ewmaRate\n456: \n457: \tmetrics  *queueManagerMetrics\n458: \tinterner *pool\n459: }\n460: \n461: // NewQueueManager builds a new QueueManager and starts a new\n462: // WAL watcher with queue manager as the WriteTo destination.\n463: // The WAL watcher takes the dir parameter as the base directory\n464: // for where the WAL shall be located. Note that the full path to\n465: // the WAL directory will be constructed as <dir>/wal.\n466: func NewQueueManager(\n467: \tmetrics *queueManagerMetrics,\n468: \twatcherMetrics *wlog.WatcherMetrics,\n469: \treaderMetrics *wlog.LiveReaderMetrics,\n470: \tlogger *slog.Logger,\n471: \tdir string,\n472: \tcfg config.QueueConfig,\n473: \tmCfg config.MetadataConfig,\n474: \texternalLabels labels.Labels,\n475: \trelabelConfigs []*relabel.Config,\n476: \tclient WriteClient,\n477: \tflushDeadline time.Duration,\n478: \tinterner *pool,\n479: \tsm ReadyScrapeManager,\n480: \tenableExemplarRemoteWrite bool,\n481: \tenableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite bool,\n482: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool,\n483: \tprotoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg,\n484: ) *QueueManager {\n485: \tif logger == nil {\n486: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n487: \t}\n488: \n489: \t// Copy externalLabels into a slice, which we need for processExternalLabels.\n490: \textLabelsSlice := make([]labels.Label, 0, externalLabels.Len())\n491: \texternalLabels.Range(func(l labels.Label) {\n492: \t\textLabelsSlice = append(extLabelsSlice, l)\n493: \t})\n494: \n495: \tlogger = logger.With(remoteName, client.Name(), endpoint, client.Endpoint())\n496: \tt := &QueueManager{\n497: \t\tlogger:                  logger,\n498: \t\tflushDeadline:           flushDeadline,\n499: \t\tcfg:                     cfg,\n500: \t\tmcfg:                    mCfg,\n501: \t\texternalLabels:          extLabelsSlice,\n502: \t\trelabelConfigs:          relabelConfigs,\n503: \t\tstoreClient:             client,\n504: \t\tsendExemplars:           enableExemplarRemoteWrite,\n505: \t\tsendNativeHistograms:    enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite,\n506: \t\tenableTypeAndUnitLabels: enableTypeAndUnitLabels,\n507: \n508: \t\tseriesLabels:         make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]labels.Labels),\n509: \t\tseriesMetadata:       make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]*metadata.Metadata),\n510: \t\tseriesSegmentIndexes: make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int),\n511: \t\tdroppedSeries:        make(map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]struct{}),\n512: \t\tbuilder:              labels.NewBuilder(labels.EmptyLabels()),\n513: \n514: \t\tnumShards:   cfg.MinShards,\n515: \t\treshardChan: make(chan int),\n516: \t\tquit:        make(chan struct{}),\n517: \n518: \t\tdataIn:          newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n519: \t\tdataOut:         newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n520: \t\tdataOutDuration: newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration),\n521: \n522: \t\tmetrics:  metrics,\n523: \t\tinterner: interner,\n524: \n525: \t\tprotoMsg: protoMsg,\n526: \t\tcompr:    compression.Snappy, // Hardcoded for now, but scaffolding exists for likely future use.\n527: \t}\n528: \n529: \twalMetadata := t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1\n530: \n531: \tt.watcher = wlog.NewWatcher(watcherMetrics, readerMetrics, logger, client.Name(), t, dir, enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n532: \n533: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n534: \t// with the new approach, which stores metadata as WAL records and\n535: \t// ships them alongside series. If both mechanisms are set, the new one\n536: \t// takes precedence by implicitly disabling the older one.\n537: \tif t.mcfg.Send && t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n538: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"usage of 'metadata_config.send' is redundant when using remote write v2 (or higher) as metadata will always be gathered from the WAL and included for every series within each write request\")\n539: \t\tt.mcfg.Send = false\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n543: \t\tt.metadataWatcher = NewMetadataWatcher(logger, sm, client.Name(), t, t.mcfg.SendInterval, flushDeadline)\n544: \t}\n545: \tt.shards = t.newShards()\n546: \n547: \treturn t\n548: }\n549: \n550: // AppendWatcherMetadata sends metadata to the remote storage. Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := t.sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx, mm[i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend:last], pBuf)\n574: \t\tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t\tt.metrics.failedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(last - (i * t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n576: \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch: being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, The breaking changes are mainly around the removal of deprecated feature flags and CLI arguments, and the full list can be found below. For users that want to upgrade we recommend to read through our [migration guide](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/3.0/migration/).\\n195: \\n196: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMAXPROCS` variable automatically to match the Linux CPU quota. The `auto-gomaxprocs` feature flag was removed. #15376\\n197: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMEMLIMIT` variable automatically to match the Linux container memory limit. Use `--no-auto-gomemlimit` to disable it. Add ability to specify a `fallback_scrape_protocol` in the scrape config. #15136\\n199: * [CHANGE] Remote-write: default enable_http2 to false. #15219\\n200: * [CHANGE] Scraping: normalize \\\"le\\\" and \\\"quantile\\\" label values upon ingestion. #15164\\n201: * [CHANGE] Scraping: config `scrape_classic_histograms` was renamed to `always_scrape_classic_histograms`. #15178\\n202: * [CHANGE] Config: remove expand-external-labels flag, expand external labels env vars by default. #14657\\n203: * [CHANGE] Disallow configuring AM with the v1 api. #13883\\n204: * [CHANGE] regexp `.` now matches all characters (performance improvement). #14505\\n205: * [CHANGE] `holt_winters` is now called `double_exponential_smoothing` and moves behind the [experimental-promql-functions feature flag](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/latest/feature_flags/#experimental-promql-functions). #14930\\n206: * [CHANGE] API: The OTLP receiver endpoint can now be enabled using `--web.enable-otlp-receiver` instead of `--enable-feature=otlp-write-receiver`. #14894\\n207: * [CHANGE] Prometheus will not add or remove port numbers from the target address. `no-default-scrape-port` feature flag removed. #14160\\n208: * [CHANGE] Logging: the format of log lines has changed a little, along with the adoption of Go's Structured Logging package. #14906\\n209: * [CHANGE] Don't create extra `_created` timeseries if feature-flag `created-timestamp-zero-ingestion` is enabled. #14738\\n210: * [CHANGE] Float literals and time durations being the same is now a stable fetaure. #15111\\n211: * [CHANGE] UI: The old web UI has been replaced by a completely new one that is less cluttered and adds a few new features (PromLens-style tree view, better metrics explorer, \\\"Explain\\\" tab). However, it is still missing some features of the old UI (notably, exemplar display and heatmaps). To switch back to the old UI, you can use the feature flag `--enable-feature=old-ui` for the time being. #14872\\n212: * [CHANGE] PromQL: Range selectors and the lookback delta are now left-open, i.e. a sample coinciding with the lower time limit is excluded rather than included. #13904\\n213: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of EndpointSlice. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.25. #14365\\n214: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `networking.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of Ingress. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.22. #14365\\n215: * [CHANGE] UTF-8: Enable UTF-8 support by default. Prometheus now allows all UTF-8 characters in metric and label names. The corresponding `utf8-name` feature flag has been removed. #14705, #15258\\n216: * [CHANGE] Console: Remove example files for the console feature. Users can continue using the console feature by supplying their own JavaScript and templates. #14807\\n217: * [CHANGE] SD: Enable the new service discovery manager by default. This SD manager does not restart unchanged discoveries upon reloading. This makes reloads faster and reduces pressure on service discoveries' sources. The corresponding `new-service-discovery-manager` feature flag has been removed. #14770\\n218: * [CHANGE] Agent mode has been promoted to stable. The feature flag `agent` has been removed. ## 3.0.0 / 2024-11-14\n193: \n194: This release includes new features such as a brand new UI and UTF-8 support enabled by default. As this marks the first new major version in seven years, several breaking changes are introduced. The breaking changes are mainly around the removal of deprecated feature flags and CLI arguments, and the full list can be found below. For users that want to upgrade we recommend to read through our [migration guide](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/3.0/migration/).\n195: \n196: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMAXPROCS` variable automatically to match the Linux CPU quota. Use `--no-auto-gomaxprocs` to disable it. The `auto-gomaxprocs` feature flag was removed. #15376\n197: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMEMLIMIT` variable automatically to match the Linux container memory limit. Use `--no-auto-gomemlimit` to disable it. The `auto-gomemlimit` feature flag was removed. #15373\n198: * [CHANGE] Scraping: Remove implicit fallback to the Prometheus text format in case of invalid/missing Content-Type and fail the scrape instead.   "content": "# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Prometheus remote-write queue system experiences intermittent sample loss and stalled shards during dynamic resharding operations. When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)\n\nThe bug occurs at line 1241:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC\n    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n```\n\nWhen resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards\n```\n\nThe sequence creates a race condition:\n\n1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)\n   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)\n   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)\n\n2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):\n   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)\n   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)\n   - Samples in queues are lost\n\n3. **start() is called while old shards still dropping**:\n   - **Immediately resets metric: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`** (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queue array (line 1244-1246)\n   - Starts new shard goroutines (line 1263-1265)\n   - Dropped samples from old shards are never reflected in metrics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Shard Assignment Changes During Transition\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `enqueue()` (line 1312-1341)\n\nThe shard assignment is computed by: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` (line 1315)\n\nDuring resharding:\n- Old queues have count `N`\n- New queues have count `M` (where N \u2260 M due to scaling)\n- Samples that fail to enqueue during shutdown retry later\n- They now hash to potentially different shard indices\n- This can create unbalanced load or ordering issues\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code Paths\n\n**Resharding Trigger** (`queue_manager.go:1057-1082`):\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n    ...\n    case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n        t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n        t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\n**Sample Enqueueing** (`queue_manager.go:1312-1341`):\n- Line 1326: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` - increments when added\n- Line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` - **unconditionally reset!**\n- No corresponding decrement when old samples are dropped\n\n**Sample Drop Path** (`queue_manager.go:1561-1578`):\n```go\ncase <-ctx.Done():\n    droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // Only if hard shutdown\n    s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n```\n\nThe problem: When `Set(0)` is called in `start()`, this overrides any attempted decrements from old shards.\n\n### Timing Window\n\nThe issue manifests as **intermittent** because it depends on:\n1. **Resharding trigger**: Target discovery changes (add/remove targets)\n2. **Load at trigger time**: Number of samples in flight when resharding begins\n3. **Flush deadline**: Whether old queues can send all samples within timeout\n4. **Remote backend latency**: If remote storage is slow, flush times out\n\nScenarios that increase probability:\n- High sample volume during discovery change\n- Slow remote-write backend (causing sends to take > flushDeadline)\n- Frequent target discovery updates\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Package\n- **`storage/remote/`**: Queue management, resharding logic\n\n### Specific Files\n- `queue_manager.go`: Core resharding mechanism (lines 1057-1305)\n- Lines 1237-1266: `shards.start()` - the bug trigger\n- Lines 1184-1199: `reshardLoop()` - orchestrates resharding\n- Lines 1269-1305: `shards.stop()` - initiates flush/shutdown\n- Lines 1312-1341: `enqueue()` - shard assignment\n\n### Metrics Affected\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - reports 0 despite queued samples\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - transitions occur during vulnerable window\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - incomplete on timeout\n\n## Mechanism: Why Shards Stall\n\n1. **During resharding transition window**:\n   - `softShutdown` is closed in old shards (line 1275)\n   - `enqueue()` fails for new samples (line 1317-1318)\n   - No new shards exist yet (sequential: stop \u2192 start)\n\n2. **Failed samples in WAL retry loop** (line 815-866 example):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       // Retry with exponential backoff\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **When start() completes**:\n   - Retrying samples go to new queues\n   - But if new shard count differs, hash assignments change\n   - Some historical samples may hash to different (potentially saturated) shards\n\n4. **Result**:\n   - Specific shards appear stuck with `samples_pending > 0`\n   - Other shards drain normally\n   - Uneven load distribution persists\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n### Logs to Watch For\n- `\"Remote storage resharding\"` - indicates resharding started\n- `\"Currently resharding, skipping\"` - resharding in progress (from line 1076)\n- `\"Failed to flush all samples on shutdown\"` - samples dropped (from line 1299)\n- `\"enqueue_retries_total\"` increasing - samples failing to enqueue (metric)\n\n### Metrics to Correlate\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - changes during resharding\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should **not** drop to 0 during transition\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - increase during timeout\n4. `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - spikes during resharding window\n5. Query: Which shards have high pending values?\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{shard=\"X\"}` if exposed per-shard\n\n### Reproduction Conditions\n- Trigger target discovery changes while sending high sample volume\n- Configure remote backend with high latency\n- Set low `flushDeadline` in config\n- Monitor metrics during target add/remove operations\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Option 1: Atomic Metric Update (Recommended)**\n- Track pending samples from old shards before reset\n- Only reset new shards' metrics\n- Don't call `Set(0)` unconditionally\n\n**Option 2: Prevent Resharding During Flush**\n- Don't trigger new resharding until old shards fully shutdown\n- Wait for `s.done` channel before calling `start()`\n- Currently already done sequentially, so issue is timing\n\n**Option 3: Increase Flush Timeout**\n- Current default `flushDeadline` may be too aggressive\n- Extend to allow slow backends to drain queues\n- Less ideal: masks the real issue\n\n### Diagnostic Steps for Root Cause Confirmation\n\n1. **Query metrics during target discovery change**:\n   ```\n   # Watch when resharding starts\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards\n\n   # Should NOT drop to 0 mid-resharding\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n\n   # Count dropped samples\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total\n   ```\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in remote storage:\n   - Check logs for \"Resharding done\" log message\n   - Verify samples_pending > 0 at that point\n   - If pending drops to 0 immediately after, bug confirmed\n\n3. **Trace queue depth**:\n   - Check old shard queue lengths before stop()\n   - Check if samples appear in queued-but-dropped metrics\n   - Correlate timestamp of resharding with metric spikes\n\n4. **Check remote backend latency**:\n   - If backend slowness triggered timeout, check remote latency metrics\n   - Confirm `flushDeadline` is insufficient for current backend\n\n## Related Issues\n\n- CHANGELOG #13562: \"Disable resharding during active retry backoffs\"\n- CHANGELOG #7122: \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\"\n- These suggest this is a known challenging area with prior bugs\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe intermittent sample loss during resharding is caused by unconditionally resetting the `pendingSamples` metric while old queue shards are still in the process of flushing (and potentially timing out and hard-shutting down). The metric reset hides dropped samples, and the shard reassignment during the vulnerable window creates asymmetric load on new shards, causing some to appear stalled. The issue is intermittent because it depends on the timing of target discovery changes relative to ongoing sample processing and remote backend latency.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

## Summary

The Prometheus remote-write queue system experiences intermittent sample loss and stalled shards during dynamic resharding operations. When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.

## Root Cause

### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush

**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)

The bug occurs at line 1241:
```go
func (s *shards) start(n int) {
    s.mtx.Lock()
    defer s.mtx.Unlock()

    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC
    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))
```

When resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):
```go
case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:
    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards
    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards
```

The sequence creates a race condition:

1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):
   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)
   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)
   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)

2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):
   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)
   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)
   - Samples in queues are lost

3. **start() is called while old shards still dropping**:
   - **Immediately resets metric: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`** (line 1241)
   - Creates new queue array (line 1244-1246)
   - Starts new shard goroutines (line 1263-1265)
   - Dropped samples from old shards are never reflected in metrics

#
... (truncated)
